null : currentTransactionHolder.handle;\\n156:     }\\n157: \\n158:     @Nonnull\\n159:     protected Stream<Map.Entry<Long, TXN>> pendingTransactions() {\\n160:         return pendingCommitTransactions.entrySet().stream()\\n161:                 .map(e -> new AbstractMap.SimpleEntry<>(e.getKey(), e.getValue().handle));\\n162:     }\\n163: \\n164:     // ------ methods that should be implemented in child class to support two phase commit\\n165:     // algorithm ------\\n166: \\n167:     /** Write value within a transaction. */\\n168:     protected abstract void invoke(TXN transaction, IN value, Context context) throws Exception;\\n169: \\n170:     /**\\n171:      * Method that starts a new transaction.\\n172:      *\\n173:      * @return newly created transaction.\\n174:      */\\n175:     protected abstract TXN beginTransaction() throws Exception;\\n176: \\n177:     /**\\n178:      * Pre commit previously created transaction. After this point the\\n180:      * transaction might still be aborted, but underlying implementation must ensure that commit\\n181:      * calls on already pre committed transactions will always succeed.\\n182:      *\\n183:      * <p>Usually implementation involves flushing the data.\\n184:      */\\n185:     protected abstract void preCommit(TXN transaction) throws Exception;\\n186: \\n187:     /**\\n188:      * Commit a pre-committed transaction. If this method fail, Flink application will be restarted\\n189:      * and {@link TwoPhaseCommitSinkFunction#recoverAndCommit(Object)} will be called again for the\\n190:      * same transaction.\\n191:      */\\n192:     protected abstract void commit(TXN transaction);\\n193: \\n194:     /**\\n195:      * Invoked on recovered transactions after a failure. User implementation must ensure that this\\n196:      * call will eventually succeed. If it fails, Flink application will be restarted and it will be\\n197:      * invoked again. If it does not succeed eventually, a data loss will occur. Transactions will\\n198:      * be recovered in an order in which they were created.\\n199:      */\\n200:     protected void recoverAndCommit(TXN transaction) {\\n201:         commit(transaction);\\n202:     }\\n203: \\n204:     /** Abort a transaction. */\\n205:     protected abstract void abort(TXN transaction);\\n206: \\n207:     /** Abort a transaction that was rejected by a coordinator after a failure. */\\n208:     protected void recoverAndAbort(TXN transaction) {\\n209:         abort(transaction);\\n210:     }\\n211: \\n212:     /**\\n213:      * Callback for subclasses which is called after restoring (each) user context.\\n214:      *\\n215:      * @param handledTransactions transactions which were already committed or aborted and do not\\n216:      *     need further handling\\n217:      */\\n218:     protected void finishRecoveringContext(Collection<TXN> handledTransactions) {}\\n219: \\n220:     /**\\n221:      * This method is called at the end of data processing.\\n222:      *\\n223:      * <p>The method is expected to flush all remaining buffered data. Exceptions will cause the\\n224:      * pipeline to be recognized as failed, because the last data items are not processed properly.\\n225:      * You may use this method to flush remaining buffered elements in the state into the current\\n226:      * transaction which will be committed in the last checkpoint.\\n227:      */\\n228:     protected void finishProcessing(@Nullable TXN transaction) {}\\n229: \\n230:     // ------ entry points for above methods implementing {@CheckPointedFunction} and\\n231:     // {@CheckpointListener} ------\\n232: \\n233:     /** This should not be implemented by subclasses. */\\n234:     @Override\\n235:     public final void invoke(IN value) throws Exception {}\\n236: \\n237:     @Override\\n238:     public final void invoke(IN value, Context context) throws Exception {\\n239:         TXN currentTransaction = currentTransaction();\\n240:         checkNotNull(\\n241:                 currentTransaction,\\n242:                 \\\"Two phase commit sink function with null transaction should not be invoked! \\\");\\n243:         invoke(currentTransaction, value, context);\\n244:     }\\n245: \\n246:     @Override\\n247:     public final void finish() throws Exception {\\n248:         finished = true;\\n249:         finishProcessing(currentTransaction());\\n250:     }\\n251: \\n252:     @Override\\n253:     public final void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {\\n254:         // the following scenarios are possible here\\n255:         //\\n256:         //  (1) there is exactly one transaction from the latest checkpoint that\\n257:         //      was triggered and completed. That should be the common case.\\n258:         //      Simply commit that transaction in that case.\\n259:         //\\n260:         //  (2) there are multiple pending transactions because one previous\\n261:         //      checkpoint was skipped. That is a rare case, but can happen\\n262:         //      for example when:\\n263:         //\\n264:         //        - the master cannot persist the metadata of the last\\n265:         //          checkpoint (temporary outage in the storage system) but\\n266:         //          could persist a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\\n267:         //\\n268:         //        - other tasks could not persist their status during\\n269:         //          the previous checkpoint, but did not trigger a failure because they\\n270:         //          could hold onto their state and could successfully persist it in\\n271:         //          a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\\n272:         //\\n273:         //      In both cases, the prior checkpoint never reach a committed state, but\\n274:         //      this checkpoint is always expected to subsume the prior one and cover all\\n275:         //      changes since the last successful one. As a consequence, we need to commit\\n276:         //      all pending transactions.\\n277:         //\\n278:         //  (3) Multiple transactions are pending, but the checkpoint complete notification\\n279:         //      relates not to the latest. That is possible, because notification messages\\n280:         //      can be delayed (in an extreme case till arrive after a succeeding checkpoint\\n281:         //      was triggered) and because there can be concurrent overlapping checkpoints\\n282:         //      (a new one is started before the previous fully finished).\\n283:         //\\n284:         // ==> There should never be a case where we have no pending transaction here\\n285:         //\\n286: \\n287:         Iterator<Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>>> pendingTransactionIterator =\\n288:                 pendingCommitTransactions.entrySet().iterator();\\n289:         Throwable firstError = null;\\n290: \\n291:         while (pendingTransactionIterator.hasNext()) {\\n292:             Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>> entry = pendingTransactionIterator.next();\\n293:             Long pendingTransactionCheckpointId = entry.getKey();\\n294:             TransactionHolder<TXN> pendingTransaction = entry.getValue();\\n295:             if (pendingTransactionCheckpointId > checkpointId) {\\n296:                 continue;\\n297:             }\\n298: \\n299:             LOG.info(\\n300:                     \\\"{} - checkpoint {} complete, committing transaction {} from checkpoint {}\\\",\\n301:                     name(),\\n302:                     checkpointId,\\n303:                     pendingTransaction,\\n304:                     pendingTransactionCheckpointId);\\n305: \\n306:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(pendingTransaction);\\n307:             try {\\n308:                 commit(pendingTransaction.handle);\\n309:             } catch (Throwable t) {\\n310:                 if (firstError == null) {\\n311:                     firstError = t;\\n312:                 }\\n313:             }\\n314: \\n315:             LOG.debug(\\\"{} - committed checkpoint transaction {}\\\", name(), pendingTransaction);\\n316: \\n317:             pendingTransactionIterator.remove();\\n318:         }\\n319: \\n320:         if (firstError != null) {\\n321:             throw new FlinkRuntimeException(\\n322:                     \\\"Committing one of transactions failed, logging first encountered failure\\\",\\n323:                     firstError);\\n324:         }\\n325:     }\\n326: \\n327:     @Override\\n328:     public void notifyCheckpointAborted(long checkpointId) {}\\n329: \\n330:     @Override\\n331:     public void snapshotState(FunctionSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\\n332:         // this is like the pre-commit of a 2-phase-commit transaction\\n333:         // we are ready to commit and remember the transaction\\n334: \\n335:         long checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId();\\n336:         LOG.debug(\\n337:                 \\\"{} - checkpoint {} triggered, flushing transaction '{}'\\\",\\n338:                 name(),\\n339:                 context.getCheckpointId(),\\n340:                 currentTransactionHolder);\\n341: \\n342:         if (currentTransactionHolder != null) {\\n343:             preCommit(currentTransactionHolder.handle);\\n344: }\\n347: \\n348:         // no need to start new transactions after sink function is closed (no more input data)\\n349:         if (!finished) {\\n350:             currentTransactionHolder = beginTransactionInternal();\\n351:         } else {\\n352:             currentTransactionHolder = null;\\n353:         }\\n354:         LOG.debug(\\\"{} - started new transaction '{}'\\\", name(), currentTransactionHolder);\\n355: \\n356:         state.update(\\n357:                 Collections.singletonList(\\n358:                         new State<>(\\n359:                                 this.currentTransactionHolder,\\n360:                                 new ArrayList<>(pendingCommitTransactions.values()),\\n361:                                 userContext)));\\n362:     }\\n363: \\n364:     @Override\\n365:     public void initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext context) throws Exception {\\n366:         // when we are restoring state with pendingCommitTransactions, we don't really know whether\\n367:         // the\\n368:         // transactions were already committed, or whether there was a failure between\\n369:         // completing the checkpoint on the master, and notifying the writer here.\\n370: \\n371:         // (the common case is actually that is was already committed, the window\\n372:         // between the commit on the master and the notification here is very small)\\n373: \\n374:         // it is possible to not have any transactions at all if there was a failure before\\n375:         // the first completed checkpoint, or in case of a scale-out event, where some of the\\n376:         // new task do not have and transactions assigned to check)\\n377: \\n378:         // we can have more than one transaction to check in case of a scale-in event, or\\n379:         // for the reasons discussed in the 'notifyCheckpointComplete()' method.\\n380: \\n381:         state = context.getOperatorStateStore().getListState(stateDescriptor);\\n382: \\n383:         boolean recoveredUserContext = false;\\n384:         if (context.isRestored()) {\\n385: eventually, there is actually data loss\\n393:                     recoverAndCommitInternal(recoveredTransaction);\\n394: operatorState.getPendingTransaction());\\n407:                     }\\n408:                 }\\n409: \\n410:                 if (userContext.isPresent()) {\\n411: beginTransactionInternal() throws Exception {\\n434:         return new TransactionHolder<>(beginTransaction(), clock.millis());\\n435:     }\\n436: \\n437:     /**\\n438:      * This method must be the only place to call {@link #recoverAndCommit(Object)} to ensure that\\n439:      * the configuration parameters {@link #transactionTimeout} and {@link\\n440:      * #ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout} are respected.\\n441:      */\\n442:     private void recoverAndCommitInternal(TransactionHolder<TXN> transactionHolder) {\\n443:         try {\\n444:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(transactionHolder);\\n445:             recoverAndCommit(transactionHolder.handle);\\n446:         } catch (final Exception e) {\\n447:             final long ({}).\\\"\\n452:                                 + \\\"Commit will not be attempted again. That should be the common case.\n258:         //      Simply commit that transaction in that case.\n259:         //\n260:         //  (2) there are multiple pending transactions because one previous\n261:         //      checkpoint was skipped. That is a rare case, but can happen\n262:         //      for example when:\n263:         //\n264:         //        - the master cannot persist the metadata of the last\n265:         //          checkpoint (temporary outage in the storage system) but\n266:         //          could persist a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\n267:         //\n268:         //        - other tasks could not persist their status during\n269:         //          the previous checkpoint, but did not trigger a failure because they\n270:         //          could hold onto their state and could successfully persist it in\n271:         //          a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\n272:         //\n273:         //      In both cases, the prior checkpoint never reach a committed state, but\n274:         //      this checkpoint is always expected to subsume the prior one and cover all\n275:         //      changes since the last successful one. As a consequence, we need to commit\n276:         //      all pending transactions.\n277:         //\n278:         //  (3) Multiple transactions are pending, but the checkpoint complete notification\n279:         //      relates not to the latest. That is possible, because notification messages\n280:         //      can be delayed (in an extreme case till arrive after a succeeding checkpoint\n281:         //      was triggered) and because there can be concurrent overlapping checkpoints\n282:         //      (a new one is started before the previous fully finished).\n283:         //\n284:         // ==> There should never be a case where we have no pending transaction here\n285:         //\n286: \n287:         Iterator<Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>>> pendingTransactionIterator =\n288:                 pendingCommitTransactions.entrySet().iterator();\n289:         Throwable firstError = null;\n290: \n291:         while (pendingTransactionIterator.hasNext()) {\n292:             Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>> entry = pendingTransactionIterator.next();\n293:             Long pendingTransactionCheckpointId = entry.getKey();\n294:             TransactionHolder<TXN> pendingTransaction = entry.getValue();\n295:             if (pendingTransactionCheckpointId > checkpointId) {\n296:                 continue;\n297:             }\n298: \n299:             LOG.info(\n300:                     \"{} - checkpoint {} complete, committing transaction {} from checkpoint {}\",\n301:                     name(),\n302:                     checkpointId,\n303:                     pendingTransaction,\n304:                     pendingTransactionCheckpointId);\n305: \n306:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(pendingTransaction);\n307:             try {\n308:                 commit(pendingTransaction.handle);\n309:             } catch (Throwable t) {\n310:                 if (firstError == null) {\n311:                     firstError = t;\n312:                 }\n313:             }\n314: \n315:             LOG.debug(\"{} - This is integrated\\n55:  * with the checkpointing mechanism to provide exactly once semantics.\\n56:  *\\n57:  * <p>When creating the sink a {@code basePath} must be specified. The base directory contains one\\n58:  * directory for every bucket. The bucket directories themselves contain several part files, with at\\n59:  * least one for each parallel subtask of the sink which is writing data to that bucket. These part\\n60:  * files contain the actual output data.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The sink uses a {@link BucketAssigner} to determine in which bucket directory each element\\n63:  * should be written to inside the base directory. The {@code BucketAssigner} can, for example, use\\n64:  * time or a property of the element to determine the bucket directory. The default {@code\\n65:  * BucketAssigner} is a {@link DateTimeBucketAssigner} which will create one new bucket every hour.\\n66:  * You can specify a custom {@code BucketAssigner} using the {@code\\n67:  * setBucketAssigner(bucketAssigner)} method, after calling {@link\\n68:  * StreamingFileSink#forRowFormat(Path, Encoder)} or {@link StreamingFileSink#forBulkFormat(Path,\\n69:  * BulkWriter.Factory)}.\\n70:  *\\n71:  * <p>The names of the part files could be defined using {@link OutputFileConfig}. This\\n72:  * configuration contains a part prefix and a part suffix that will be used with the parallel\\n73:  * subtask index of the sink and a rolling counter to determine the file names. For example with a\\n74:  * prefix \\\"prefix\\\" and a suffix \\\".ext\\\", a file named {@code \\\"prefix-1-17.ext\\\"} contains the data\\n75:  * from {@code subtask 1} of the sink and is the {@code 17th} bucket created by that subtask.\\n76:  *\\n77:  * <p>Part files roll based on the user-specified {@link RollingPolicy}. The reason for this is how the sink works together with the checkpointing mechanism to\\n87:  * provide exactly-once semantics and fault-tolerance.
